# Investigation: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

**Repository:** grafana/grafana
**Task Type:** Regression Hunt (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

After upgrading Grafana from v10.3 to v10.4, some dashboards with table panels fail to render correctly. The table panel's field override configuration is silently dropped during dashboard import. Users see tables with missing column formatting (column widths, text alignment, cell display modes).

The bug only affects dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` was not explicitly set in the saved dashboard JSON. Dashboards with explicit custom config render correctly.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:
1. Which migration function is responsible for the regression
2. The exact conditional logic that fails for dashboards without explicit `defaults.custom`
3. Why dashboards with explicit `defaults.custom` are unaffected
4. Which dashboard schema version triggers the issue
5. The files and functions involved in the migration chain

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- Focus on the dashboard migration pipeline, particularly schema version handlers

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V10 migration removes the first threshold value from table panel styles when they have 3 or more thresholds.
     6→// This migration aligns with the frontend schema version 10 changes that addressed aliasYAxis changes
     7→// specifically for table panels with threshold configurations.
     8→//
     9→// Background:
    10→// In earlier versions, table panels stored threshold values as arrays with the first element representing
    11→// a baseline value that was not actually used in threshold calculations. This migration removes that
    12→// unused first element to clean up the data structure.
    13→//
    14→// Example before migration:
    15→// {
    16→//   "schemaVersion": 9,
    17→//   "panels": [
    18→//     {
    19→//       "type": "table",
    20→//       "styles": [
    21→//         {
    22→//           "thresholds": ["10", "20", "30"]
    23→//         },
    24→//         {
    25→//           "thresholds": ["100", "200", "300"]
    26→//         }
    27→//       ]
    28→//     }
    29→//   ]
    30→// }
    31→//
    32→// Example after migration:
    33→// {
    34→//   "schemaVersion": 10,
    35→//   "panels": [
    36→//     {
    37→//       "type": "table",
    38→//       "styles": [
    39→//         {
    40→//           "thresholds": ["20", "30"]
    41→//         },
    42→//         {
    43→//           "thresholds": ["200", "300"]
    44→//         }
    45→//       ]
    46→//     }
    47→//   ]
    48→// }
    49→
    50→func V10(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {
    51→	dashboard["schemaVersion"] = 10
    52→
    53→	panels, ok := dashboard["panels"].([]interface{})
    54→	if !ok {
    55→		return nil
    56→	}

   103→  updateSchema(old: any, targetSchemaVersion?: number) {
   104→    let i, j, k, n;
   105→    const oldVersion = this.dashboard.schemaVersion;
   106→    const panelUpgrades: PanelSchemeUpgradeHandler[] = [];
   107→    const finalTargetVersion = targetSchemaVersion || DASHBOARD_SCHEMA_VERSION;
   108→
   109→    if (oldVersion === finalTargetVersion) {
   110→      return;
   111→    }
   112→
   113→    // version 2 schema changes
   114→    if (oldVersion < 2 && finalTargetVersion >= 2) {
   115→      if (old.services) {
   116→        if (old.services.filter) {
   117→          this.dashboard.time = old.services.filter.time;
   118→          this.dashboard.templating.list = old.services.filter.list || [];
   119→        }
   120→      }
   121→
   122→      // we used to have graphite panel type migration logic here
   123→      // but this is handled by auto migration, see public/app/features/dashboard/state/getPanelPluginToMigrateTo.ts
   124→    }
   125→
   126→    // schema version 3 changes
   127→    if (oldVersion < 3 && finalTargetVersion >= 3) {
   128→      // Panel ID assignment is now handled by ensurePanelsHaveUniqueIds() in DashboardModel
   129→      // and the grid layout migration properly handles panels without IDs in rows
   130→    }
   131→
   132→    // schema version 4 changes
   133→    if (oldVersion < 4 && finalTargetVersion >= 4) {
   134→      // graph migration is handled through the auto migration
   135→      // see autoMigrateAngular map in public/app/features/dashboard/state/PanelModel.ts
   136→    }
   137→
   138→    if (oldVersion < 6 && finalTargetVersion >= 6) {
   139→      // move drop-downs to new schema
   140→      const annotations = find(old.pulldowns, { type: 'annotations' });

     5→// V37 normalizes legend configuration to use `showLegend` property consistently.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses inconsistencies in how legend visibility was handled.
     8→// There were two ways to hide the legend:
     9→// 1. Using displayMode: "hidden"
    10→// 2. Using showLegend: false
    11→//
    12→// The migration normalizes both approaches to use showLegend consistently:
    13→// - If displayMode is "hidden" OR showLegend is false, set displayMode to "list" and showLegend to false
    14→// - For all other existing legend objects, ensure showLegend is true
    15→//
    16→// Note: This migration only processes legend configurations that already exist as objects.
    17→// Boolean legend values are not processed by this migration.
    18→//
    19→// Example transformations:
    20→//
    21→// Before migration (hidden displayMode):
    22→//
    23→//	options: {
    24→//	  legend: {
    25→//	    displayMode: "hidden",
    26→//	    placement: "bottom"
    27→//	  }
    28→//	}
    29→//
    30→// After migration:
    31→//
    32→//	options: {
    33→//	  legend: {
    34→//	    displayMode: "list",
    35→//	    showLegend: false,
    36→//	    placement: "bottom"
    37→//	  }
    38→//	}
    39→//
    40→// Before migration (showLegend false):
    41→//
    42→//	options: {
    43→//	  legend: {
    44→//	    displayMode: "table",
    45→//	    showLegend: false
    46→//	  }
    47→//	}
    48→//
    49→// After migration:
    50→//
    51→//	options: {
    52→//	  legend: {
    53→//	    displayMode: "list",
    54→//	    showLegend: false
    55→//	  }
    56→//	}

    58→// Before migration (visible legend):
    59→//
    60→//	options: {

     1→package schemaversion
     2→
     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor
... (truncated)

   306→export const migrateTextWrapToFieldLevel = (panel: PanelModel<Partial<Options>>) => {
   307→  if (panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.wrapText !== undefined) {
   308→    // already migrated
   309→    return;
   310→  }
   311→
   312→  const legacyDefaultWrapText: boolean | undefined = panel.fieldConfig?.defaults.custom?.cellOptions?.wrapText;
   313→
   314→  panel.fieldConfig.overrides = panel.fieldConfig.overrides.map((override) => {
   315→    if (override.properties) {
   316→      override.properties = override.properties.flatMap((property) => {
   317→        if (property.id === 'custom.cellOptions' && property.value && property.value.wrapText !== undefined) {
   318→          return [
   319→            { ...property, value: { ...omit(property.value, 'wrapText') } },
   320→            { id: 'custom.wrapText', value: property.value.wrapText },
   321→          ];
   322→        }
   323→        return [property];
   324→      });
   325→    }
   326→    return override;
   327→  });
   328→
   329→  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom ?? {};
   330→  panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.wrapText = legacyDefaultWrapText;
   331→  delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions?.wrapText;
   332→
   333→  return panel;
   334→};

    19→# Breaking changes in Grafana v10.3
    20→
    21→Following are breaking changes that you should be aware of when upgrading to Grafana v10.3. Breaking changes that were introduced in release 10.2.3 are also included here and are marked with an asterisk.
    22→
    23→For our purposes, a breaking change is any change that requires users or operators to do something. This includes:
    24→
    25→- Changes in one part of the system that could cause other components to fail
    26→- Deprecations or removal of a feature
    27→- Changes to an API that could break automation
    28→- Changes that affect some plugins or functions of Grafana
    29→- Migrations that can’t be rolled back
    30→
    31→For each change, the provided information:
    32→
    33→- Helps you determine if you’re affected
    34→- Describes the change or relevant background information
    35→- Guides you in how to mitigate for the change or migrate
    36→- Provides more learning resources
    37→
    38→For release highlights and deprecations, refer to our [v10.3 What’s new](https://grafana.com/docs/grafana/<GRAFANA_VERSION>/whatsnew/whats-new-in-v10-3/). For the specific steps we recommend when you upgrade to v10.3, check out our [Upgrade guide](https://grafana.com/docs/grafana/<GRAFANA_VERSION>/upgrade-guide/upgrade-v10.3/).

     1→package schemaversion

     3→import "context"
     4→
     5→// V38 migrates table panel configuration from displayMode to the structured cellOptions format.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses limitations in the original table panel cell display configuration where
     8→// the flat displayMode string property could not accommodate the growing complexity of cell rendering
     9→// options. The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it
    10→// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.
    11→//
    12→// The migration works by:
    13→// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)
    14→// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties
    15→// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode
    16→// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path
    17→// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features
    18→//
    19→// This restructuring provides several key benefits:
    20→// - Enables mode-specific configuration options (e.g., gauge thresholds, color schemes)
    21→// - Supports future cell rendering types without breaking existing configurations
    22→// - Provides clearer separation between cell type and rendering mode
    23→// - Maintains backward compatibility while preparing for enhanced table functionality
    24→//
    25→// The migration handles special cases for legacy gauge modes and color background variants,
    26→// ensuring all existing display behaviors are preserved exactly.
    27→//
    28→// Example transfor
... (truncated)

     5→// V37 normalizes legend configuration to use `showLegend` property consistently.
     6→//
     7→// This migration addresses inconsistencies in how legend visibility was handled.
     8→// There were two ways to hide the legend:
     9→// 1. Using displayMode: "hidden"
    10→// 2. Using showLegend: false
    11→//
    12→// The migration normalizes both approaches to use showLegend consistently:
    13→// - If displayMode is "hidden" OR showLegend is false, set displayMode to "list" and showLegend to false
    14→// - For all other existing legend objects, ensure showLegend is true
    15→//
    16→// Note: This migration only processes legend configurations that already exist as objects.
    17→// Boolean legend values are not processed by this migration.
    18→//
    19→// Example transformations:
    20→//
    21→// Before migration (hidden displayMode):
    22→//
    23→//	options: {
    24→//	  legend: {
    25→//	    displayMode: "hidden",
    26→//	    placement: "bottom"
    27→//	  }
    28→//	}
    29→//
    30→// After migration:
    31→//
    32→//	options: {
    33→//	  legend: {
    34→//	    displayMode: "list",
    35→//	    showLegend: false,
    36→//	    placement: "bottom"
    37→//	  }
    38→//	}
    39→//
    40→// Before migration (showLegend false):
    41→//
    42→//	options: {
    43→//	  legend: {
    44→//	    displayMode: "table",
    45→//	    showLegend: false
    46→//	  }
    47→//	}
    48→//
    49→// After migration:
    50→//
    51→//	options: {
    52→//	  legend: {
    53→//	    displayMode: "list",
    54→//	    showLegend: false
    55→//	  }
    56→//	}

    58→// Before migration (visible legend):
    59→//
    60→//	options: {
    61→//

     1→package schemaversion

     8→// V30 upgrades value mappings and migrates tooltip options for panels.
     9→//
    10→// This migration addresses two key improvements to panel configurations:
    11→// 1. Value mappings upgrade: Converts legacy value mapping format to the new structured format
    12→// 2. Tooltip options migration: Renames tooltipOptions to tooltip in specific panel types: timeseries, xychart, xychart2
    13→//
    14→// The migration works by:
    15→// 1. Iterating through all panels in the dashboard, including nested panels in collapsed rows
    16→// 2. For each panel, upgrading value mappings in fieldConfig.defaults and fieldConfig.overrides
    17→// 3. Migrating tooltip options for timeseries, xychart, and xychart2 panels
    18→// 4. Preserving all other panel configurations and options
    19→//
    20→// Value Mappings Migration:
    21→// - Converts legacy mapping types (1 = ValueToText, 2 = RangeToText) to new format
    22→// - Handles special "null" values by converting them to SpecialValue mappings
    23→// - Preserves threshold colors when available
    24→// - Consolidates multiple value mappings into a single ValueToText mapping
    25→// - Maintains range mappings as separate RangeToText mappings
    26→//
    27→// Tooltip Options Migration:
    28→// - Renames panel.options.tooltipOptions to panel.options.tooltip
    29→// - Only applies to timeseries, xychart, and xychart2 panel types
    30→// - Preserves all tooltip configuration options
    31→//
    32→// Example value mappings transformation:
    33→//
    34→// Before migration:
    35→//
    36→//	panel: {
    37→//	  "fieldConfig": {
    38→//	    "defaults": {
    39→//	      "mappings":
... (truncated)

155-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive investigation of the Grafana dashboard migration v38 table panel regression. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Investigation Complete ✓

**Report Location**: `/logs/agent/investigation.md`

### Key Findings:

**Root Cause**: The v38 schema migration contains broken conditional logic that skips processing entirely when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` doesn't exist in a dashboard's JSON.

**The Specific Problem**:
- **Backend** (`v38.go`, lines 115-137): Uses a type assertion that fails silently when `custom` object is missing, causing the entire panel migration to be skipped
- **Frontend** (`DashboardMigrator.ts`, lines 644-674): Uses optional chaining that skips defaults migration when `custom` is missing

**Why It Only Affects Dashboards Without Explicit `defaults.custom`**:
- When `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` IS explicitly defined, the migration works correctly
- When `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is missing (common in older dashboards with minimal configurations), the migration skips to the next panel without migrating field overrides
- The default `fieldConfig` structure (defined in `PanelModel.ts`) only initializes `defaults: {}` with no `custom` object

**The Silent Failure**:
The migration doesn't error—it just silently skips processing, leaving `displayMode` un-migrated to `cellOptions`, which causes field override configuration to be lost, resulting in missing column formatting.

**Evidence**:
- All test cases in `v38_test.go` have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` defined—there's no test for the failing scenario
- Earlier migrations (v30, v35) handle missing objects gracefully; v38 breaks this pattern
- The test gap directly correlates with the regression

The report in `/logs/agent/investigation.md` contains comp

[Backend Migration Tests](#backend-migration-tests)\n    31\u2192  - [Frontend Migration Comparison Tests](#frontend-migration-comparison-tests)\n    32\u2192  - [Single Version Migration Testing](#single-version-migration-testing)\n    33\u2192- [Resources](#resources)\n    34\u2192- [Getting Help](#getting-help)\n    35\u2192\n    36\u2192## Overview\n    37\u2192\n    38\u2192Dashboard schema migrations ensure backward compatibility as the dashboard data model evolves. Each migration transforms dashboards from one schema version to the next, allowing older dashboards to work with newer Grafana versions.\n    39\u2192\n    40\u2192## Current Schema Versions\n    41\u2192\n    42\u2192- **Minimum Version**: 13\n    43\u2192- **Latest Version**: 42\n    44\u2192- **Backend Location**: `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/`\n    45\u2192- **Frontend Location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`\n    46\u2192\n    47\u2192## Creating a New Migration\n    48\u2192\n    49\u2192### Step 1: Create the Migration File\n    50\u2192\n    51\u2192Create a new file: `v{N}.go` where `{N}` is the target schema version.\n    52\u2192\n    53\u2192```go\n    54\u2192package schemaversion\n    55\u2192\n    56\u2192import \"context\"\n    57\u2192\n    58\u2192// V{N} migrates [describe what this migration does].\n    59\u2192//\n    60\u2192// [Detailed description of the migration including:]\n    61\u2192// - What properties are being changed\n    62\u2192// - Why the migration is necessary\n    63\u2192// - Any special handling or edge cases\n    64\u2192//\n    65\u2192// Example before migration:\n    66\u2192//\n    67\u2192//\t\"panels\": [\n    68\u2192//\t  {\n    69\u2192//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    70\u2192//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    71\u2192//\t    \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n    72\u2192//\t  }\n    73\u2192//\t]\n    74\u2192//\n    75\u2192// Example after migration:\n    76\u2192//\n    77\u2192//\t\"panels\": [\n    78\u2192//\t  {\n    79\u2192//\t    \"id\": 1,\n    80\u2192//\t    \"type\": \"graph\",\n    81\u2192//\t    \"newProperty\": \"value\"\n    82\u2192//\t  }\n    83\u2192//\t]\n    84\u2192func V{N}(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n    85\u2192\tdashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = {N}\n    86\u2192\n    87\u2192\t// Your migration logic here\n    88\u2192\t// Transform dashboard properties as needed\n    89\u2192\n    90\u2192\treturn nil\n    91\u2192}\n    92\u2192```\n    93\u2192\n    94\u2192### Step 2: Register the Migration\n    95\u2192\n    96\u2192Add your migration to `migrations.go`:\n    97\u2192\n    98\u2192```go\n    99\u2192func GetMigrations(dsInfoProvider DataSourceInfoProvider) map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc {\n   100\u2192\treturn map[int]SchemaVersionMigrationFunc{\n   101\u2192\t\t// ... existing migrations\n   102\u2192\t\t{N}: V{N},  // Add your migration here\n   103\u2192\t\t// ... rest of migrations\n   104\u2192\t}\n   105\u2192}\n   106\u2192```\n   107\u2192\n   108\u2192### Step 3: Create Test Data\n   109\u2192\n   110\u2192#### Input Test File\n   111\u2192Create `testdata/input/v{N}.{name}.json` with schema version `{N-1}` with scenarios to cover the specific migration:\n   112\u2192\n   113\u2192```json\n   114\u2192{\n   115\u2192  \"title\": \"V{N} Migration Test Dashboard\",\n   116\u2192  \"schemaVersion\": {N-1},\n   117\u2192  \"panels\": [\n   118\u2192    {\n   119\u2192      \"id\": 1,\n   120\u2192      \"type\": \"graph\",\n   121\u2192      \"title\": \"Test Panel\",\n   122\u2192      \"oldProperty\": \"value\"\n   123\u2192    }\n   124\u2192  ]\n   125\u2192}\n   126\u2192```\n   127\u2192\n   128\u2192#### Expected Output\n   129\u2192The test system will generate `testdata/output/latest_version/v{N}.{name}.v42.json` automatically.\n   130\u2192\n   131\u2192### Step 4: Run Tests\n   132\u2192\n   133\u2192```bash\n   134\u2192# Run migration tests\n   135\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n   136\u2192\n   137\u2192# Run specific migration test\n   138\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n   139\u2192```\n   140\u2192\n   141\u2192For comprehensive testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   142\u2192\n   143\u2192### Step 5: Frontend-Backend Consistency Validation\n   144\u2192\n   145\u2192Implement different changes in the migration until frontend matches exactly with the backend side. Add as many scenarios as possible to ensure comprehensive coverage of all use cases.\n   146\u2192\n   147\u2192For detailed testing strategies including single version tests, frontend comparison tests, and full pipeline testing, see the [Comprehensive Testing Strategy](#comprehensive-testing-strategy) section.\n   148\u2192\n   149\u2192#### Test Scenarios to Cover\n   150\u2192\n   151\u2192**Panel-Level Changes:**\n   152\u2192- Panels with different types (graph, table, stat, etc.)\n   153\u2192- Panels with nested panels (rows)\n   154\u2192- Panels with various property combinations\n   155\u2192- Panels with missing or null properties\n   156\u2192- Panels with deprecated properties\n   157\u2192\n   158\u2192**Dashboard-Level Changes:**\n   159\u2192- Dashboard properties (title, tags, time, etc.)\n   160\u2192- Templating variables (query, textbox, custom, etc.)\n   161\u2192- Annotations and links\n   162\u2192- Time picker settings\n   163\u2192- Refresh settings\n   164\u2192\n   165\u2192**Edge Cases:**\n   166\u2192- Empty dashboards\n   167\u2192- Dashboards with only rows\n   168\u2192- Dashboards with mixed panel types\n   169\u2192- Dashboards with complex nested structures\n   170\u2192- Dashboards with invalid or malformed data\n   171\u2192\n   172\u2192**Property Transformations:**\n   173\u2192- Property renaming scenarios\n   174\u2192- Property type conversions\n   175\u2192- Property value transformations\n   176\u2192- Property removal scenarios\n   177\u2192- Property addition scenarios\n   178\u2192\n   179\u2192#### Validation Process\n   180\u2192\n   181\u21921. **Create comprehensive test data** covering all scenarios\n   182\u21922. **Run backend migration** and capture output\n   183\u21923. **Run frontend migration** and capture output\n   184\u21924. **Compare outputs** using strict equality checks\n   185\u21925. **Iterate on migration logic** until outputs match exactly\n   186\u21926. **Add more test cases** for any discrepancies found\n   187\u2192\n   188\u2192#### Test Data Requirements\n   189\u2192\n   190\u2192Create multiple test files for each migration:\n   191\u2192- `v{N}.basic.{name}.json` - Basic functionality\n   192\u2192- `v{N}.edge_cases.{name}.json` - Edge cases and error conditions\n   193\u2192- `v{N}.complex.{name}.json` - Complex dashboard structures\n   194\u2192- `v{N}.property_changes.{name}.json` - Property transformation scenarios\n   195\u2192\n   196\u2192### Step 6: Unit Testing\n   197\u2192\n   198\u2192Add comprehensive unit tests for both backend and frontend migrations to ensure the correct logic is implemented.\n   199\u2192\n   200\u2192#### Backend Unit Tests\n   201\u2192\n   202\u2192Create unit tests in `v{N}_test.go`:\n   203\u2192\n   204\u2192```go\n   205\u2192package schemaversion_test\n   206\u2192\n   207\u2192import (\n   208\u2192\t\"context\"\n   209\u2192\t\"testing\"\n 229\u2192\t\t\t\t\t},\n   230\u2192\t\t\t\t},\n   231\u2192\t\t\t},\n   232\u2192\t\t\texpected: map[string]interface{}{\n   233\u2192\t\t\t\t\"schemaVersion\": {N},\n   234\u2192\t\t\t\t\"panels\": []interface{}{\n   235\u2192\t\t\t\t\tmap[string]interface{}{\n   236\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t\"id\": 1,\n   237\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t\"type\": \"graph\",\n   238\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t\"newProperty\": \"value\",\n   239\u2192\t\t\t\t\t},\n   240\u2192\t\t\t\t},\n   241\u2192\t\t\t},\n   242\u2192\t\t},\n   243\u2192\t\t{\n   244\u2192\t\t\tname: \"edge case - missing property\",\n   245\u2192\t\t\tinput: 259\u2192\t\t\t\t\t\t\"type\": \"graph\",\n   260\u2192\t\t\t\t\t},\n   261\u2192\t\t\t\t},\n   262\u2192\t\t\t},\n   263\u2192\t\t},\n   264\u2192\t\t// Add more test cases...\n   265\u2192\t}\n   266\u2192\n   267\u2192\tfor _, tt := range tests {\n   268\u2192\t\tt.Run(tt.name, func(t *testing.T) {\n   269\u2192\t\t\terr := schemaversion.V{N}(context.Background(), tt.input)\n   270\u2192\t\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n   271\u2192\t\t\trequire.Equal(t, tt.expected, tt.input)\n   272\u2192\t\t})\n   273\u2192\t}\n   274\u2192}\n   275\u2192```\n   276\u2192\n   277\u2192#### Frontend Unit Tests\n   278\u2192\n   279\u2192Create unit tests in `DashboardMigrator.test.ts`:\n   280\u2192\n   281\u2192```typescript\n   282\u2192describe('V{N} Migration', () => {\n   283\u2192     id: 1,\n   289\u2192          type: 'graph',\n   290\u2192          oldProperty: 'value'\n   291\u2192        }\n   292\u2192      ]\n   293\u2192    };\n   294\u2192\n   295\u2192    const model = new DashboardModel(dashboard);\n   296\u2192    expect(model.schemaVersion).toBe({N});\n   297\u2192    expect(model.panels[0].newProperty).toBe('value');\n   298\u2192    expect(model.panels[0].oldProperty).toBeUndefined();\n   299\u2192  });\n   300\u2192\n   301\u2192  it('should handle edge cases correctly', () => {\n   302\u2192    const dashboard = {\n   303\u2192 expect(model.schemaVersion).toBe({N});\n   309\u2192    expect(model.panels).toEqual([]);\n   310\u2192  });\n   311\u2192\n   312\u2192  // Add more test cases...\n   313\u2192});\n   314\u2192```\n -run TestV{N}\n   322\u2192\n   323\u2192# Frontend unit tests\n   324\u2192yarn test DashboardMigrator.test.ts -t \"V{N}\"\n   325\u2192\n   326\u2192# Integration tests\n   327\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n   328\u2192yarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\n   329\u2192```\n   330\u2192\n   331\u2192\n   332\u2192\n   333\u2192## Utility Functions\n   334\u2192\n   335\u2192### Type Conversion\n   336\u2192```go\n   337\u2192// Convert various types to float64\n   338\u2192func ConvertToFloat(value interface{}) (float64, bool) {\n   339\u2192\t// Implementation in utils.go\n   340\u2192}\n   341\u2192\n   342\u2192// Get string value with default\n   343\u2192func GetStringValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string, defaultValue string) string {\n   344\u2192\t// Implementation in utils.go\n   345\u2192}\n   346\u2192\n   347\u2192// Get boolean value with default\n   348\u2192func GetBoolValue(data map[string]interface{}, key string) bool {\n   349\u2192\t// Implementation in utils.go\n   350\u2192}\n   351\u2192```\n   352\u2192\n   353\u2192### Data Access\n   354\u2192```go\n   355\u2192// Safe property access\n   356\u2192if value, ok := panel[\"property\"].(string); ok {\n   357\u2192\t// Use value\n   358\u2192}\n   359\u2192\n   360\u2192// Safe array access\n   361\u2192if panels, ok := dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n   362\u2192\t// Process panels\n   363\u2192}\n   364\u2192```\n   365\u2192\n   366\u2192## Common Pitfalls\n   367\u2192\n   368\u2192### 1. Type Assertions\n   369\u2192```go\n   370\u2192// \u274c Wrong - can panic\n   371\u2192value := panel[\"property\"].(string)\n   372\u2192\n   373\u2192// \u2705 Correct - safe type assertion\n   374\u2192if value, ok := panel[\"property\"].(string); ok {\n   375\u2192\t// Use value\n   376\u2192}\n   377\u2192```\n   378\u2192\n   379\u2192### 2. Null Handling\n   380\u2192```go\n   381\u2192// \u274c Wrong - removes intentional nulls\n   382\u2192if value == nil {\n   383\u2192\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   384\u2192}\n   385\u2192\n   386\u2192// \u2705 Correct - preserve intentional nulls\n   387\u2192if value == nil && !isIntentionallyNull(panel, \"property\") {\n   388\u2192\tdelete(panel, \"property\")\n   389\u2192}\n   390\u2192```\n   391\u2192\n   392\u2192### 3. Nested Panel Processing\n   393\u2192```go\n   394\u2192// \u274c Wrong - misses nested panels\n   395\u2192for _, panel := range panels {\n   396\u2192\tmigratePanel(panel)\n   397\u2192}\n   398\u2192\n   399\u2192// \u2705 Correct - handles nested panels\n   400\u2192for _, panel := range panels {\n   401\u2192\tmigratePanelRecursively(panel)\n   402\u2192}\n   403\u2192```\n   404\u2192\n   405\u2192## Migration Beyond v42\n   406\u2192\n   407\u2192**Important**: Schema version 42 is the final version for the v1 dashboard API. For new migrations beyond v42:\n   408\u2192\n   409\u21921. **Backend**: Continue adding schema versions in Go\n   410\u21922. **Frontend**: Use panel-specific migration handlers instead of schema versions\n   411\u21923. **Justification Required**: Each new migration must be properly justified\n   412\u21924. **v2 Transition**: Consider the impact on the transition to schema v2\n   413\u2192\n   414\u2192### When to Add Schema Migrations vs Panel Migrations\n   415\u2192\n   416\u2192**Add Schema Migration** when:\n   417\u2192- Changes affect dashboard-level properties\n   418\u2192- Cross-panel transformations are needed\n   419\u2192- Backward compatibility requires schema version increment\n   420\u2192- **With proper justification** about why it can't be handled as panel migration\n   421\u2192\n   422\u2192**Use Panel-Specific Migrations** when:\n   423\u2192- Changes are panel-type specific\n   424\u2192- Can be handled within individual panel plugins\n   425\u2192- Don't require dashboard-level schema changes\n   426\u2192\n   427\u2192## Testing Guidelines\n   428\u2192\n   429\u2192### Test File Naming\n   430\u2192- Input: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.json`\n   431\u2192- Output: `v{N}.{descriptive_name}.v42.json`\n   432\u2192\n   433\u2192### Test Data Requirements\n   434\u2192- Input schema version should be `{N-1}`\n   435\u2192- Include comprehensive test cases\n   436\u2192- Test edge cases and error conditions\n   437\u2192- Use realistic dashboard data\n   438\u2192\n   439\u2192### Running Tests\n   440\u2192```bash\n   441\u2192# Run all migration tests\n   442\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/...\n   443\u2192\n   444\u2192# Run specific test\n   445\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n   446\u2192\n   447\u2192# Run with verbose output\n   448\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -v\n   449\u2192```\n   450\u2192\n   451\u2192## Comprehensive Testing Strategy\n   452\u2192\n   453\u2192### Backend Migration Tests\n   454\u2192\n   455\u2192The backend migration tests validate schema version migrations and API conversions:\n   456\u2192\n   457\u2192- **Schema migration tests**: Test individual schema version upgrades (v14\u2192v15, v15\u2192v16, etc.)\n   458\u2192- **Conversion tests**: Test API version conversions with automatic metrics instrumentation\n   459\u2192- **Test data**: Uses curated test files from `testdata/input/` covering schema versions 14-42\n   460\u2192- **Metrics validation**: Tests verify that conversion metrics are properly recorded\n   461\u2192\n   462\u2192**Test execution:**\n   463\u2192```bash\n   464\u2192# All backend migration tests\n   465\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -v\n   466\u2192\n   467\u2192# Schema migration tests only\n   468\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/ -v\n   469\u2192\n   470\u2192# API conversion tests with metrics\n   471\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/conversion/... -v\n   472\u2192```\n   473\u2192\n   474\u2192### Frontend Migration Comparison Tests\n   475\u2192\n   476\u2192The frontend migration comparison tests validate that backend and frontend migration logic produce consistent results:\n   477\u2192\n   478\u2192- **Test methodology**: Compares backend vs frontend migration outputs through DashboardModel integration\n   479\u2192- **Dataset coverage**: Tests run against 42+ curated test files spanning schema versions 14-42\n   480\u2192- **Test location**: `public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts`\n   481\u2192- **Test data**: Located in `apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/testdata/input/` and `testdata/output/`\n   482\u2192\n   483\u2192**Test execution:**\n   484\u2192```bash\n   485\u2192# Frontend migration comparison tests\n   486\u2192yarn test DashboardMigratorToBackend.test.ts\n   487\u2192```\n   488\u2192\n   489\u2192**Test approach:**\n   490\u2192- **Frontend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 DashboardMigrator \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\n   491\u2192- **Backend path**: `jsonInput \u2192 Backend Migration \u2192 backendOutput \u2192 DashboardModel \u2192 getSaveModelClone()`\n   492\u2192- **Comparison**: Direct comparison of final migrated states from both paths\n   493\u2192\n   494\u2192### Single Version Migration Testing\n   495\u2192\n   496\u2192The system supports both single version and full pipeline testing:\n   497\u2192\n   498\u2192- **Single version tests**: Test individual migrations (v15 \u2192 v16)\n   499\u2192- **Full pipeline tests**: Test complete migration (v15 \u2192 v42)\n   500\u2192- **Test directories**: `single_version/` vs `latest_version/`\n   501\u2192- **Coverage**: Comprehensive testing of all migration paths\n   502\u2192\n   503\u2192**Test execution:**\n   504\u2192```bash\n   505\u2192# Single version migration tests\n   506\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrateSingleVersion\n   507\u2192\n   508\u2192# Full pipeline tests\n   509\u2192go test ./apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/... -run TestMigrate\n   510\u2192```\n   511\u2192\n   512\u2192## Resources\n   513\u2192\n   514\u2192- [Migration Architecture Documentation](../../../docs/migration-architecture.md)\n   515\u2192- [Frontend Migration The original design forced all display settings into a single string value, making it\n// difficult to add new customization parameters or provide mode-specific configuration options.\n//\n// The migration works by:\n// 1. Locating table panels in the dashboard (including nested panels within rows)\n// 2. Examining field configuration defaults and any field overrides for displayMode properties\n// 3. Converting string displayMode values to structured cellOptions objects with type and mode\n// 4. Updating both field defaults and field override references to use the new property path\n// 5. Preserving all existing visual behavior while enabling future cell customization features\n//\n// This restructuring provides several key benefits:\n// - Enables mode-specific configuration options Iterating through all panels in the dashboard, including nested panels in collapsed rows\n// 2. For each panel, upgrading value mappings in fieldConfig.defaults and fieldConfig.overrides\n// 3. Migrating tooltip options for timeseries, xychart, and xychart2 panels\n// 4. Preserving all other panel configurations and options\n//\n// Value Mappings Migration:\n// - Converts legacy mapping types (1 = ValueToText, 2 = RangeToText) to new format\n// - Handles special \"null\" values by converting them to SpecialValue mappings\n// - Preserves threshold colors when available\n// - Consolidates multiple value mappings into a single ValueToText mapping\n// - Maintains range mappings as separate RangeToText mappings\n//\n// Tooltip Options Migration:\n// - Renames panel.options.tooltipOptions to panel.options.tooltip\n// - Only applies to timeseries, xychart, and xychart2 panel types\n// - Preserves all tooltip configuration options\n//\n// Example value mappings transformation:\n//\n// Before migration:\n//\n//\tpanel: {\n//\t  \"fieldConfig\": {\n//\t    \"defaults\": {\n//\t      \"mappings\": [\n//\t        { \"id\": 0, \"text\": \"Up\", \"type\": 1, \"value\": \"1\" },\n//\t        { \"id\": 1, \"text\": \"Down\", \"type\": 1, \"value\": \"0\" },\n//\t        { \"from\": \"10\", \"to\": \"20\", \"text\": \"Medium\", \"type\": 2 }\n//\t      ]\n//\t    }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\n//\n// After migration:\n//\n//\tpanel: {\n//\t  \"fieldConfig\": {\n//\t    \"defaults\": {\n//\t      \"mappings\": [\n//\t        {\n//\t          \"type\": \"value\",\n//\t          \"options\": {\n//\t            \"1\": { \"text\": \"Up\" },\n//\t            \"0\": { \"text\": \"Down\" }\n//\t          }\n//\t        },\n//\t        {\n//\t          \"type\": \"range\",\n//\t          \"options\": {\n//\t            \"from\": 10,\n//\t            \"to\": 20,\n//\t            \"result\": { \"text\": \"Medium\" }\n//\t          }\n//\t        }\n//\t      ]\n//\t    }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\n//\n// Example tooltip options transformation:\n//\n// Before migration:\n//\n//\tpanel: {\n//\t  \"type\": \"timeseries\",\n//\t  \"options\": {\n//\t    \"tooltipOptions\": { \"mode\": \"multi\" }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\n//\n// After migration:\n//\n//\tpanel: {\n//\t  \"type\": \"timeseries\",\n//\t  \"options\": {\n//\t    \"tooltip\": { \"mode\": \"multi\" }\n//\t  }\n//\t}\nfunc V30(_ context.Context, dashboard map[string]interface{}) error {\n\tdashboard[\"schemaVersion\"] = 30\n\n\tpanels, ok := dashboard[\"panels\"].([]interface{})\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, panel := range panels {\n\t\tpanelMap, ok := panel.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tupgradeValueMappingsForPanel(panelMap)\n\t\tmigrateTooltipOptions(panelMap)\n\n\t\t// Handle nested panels in collapsed rows\n\t\tnestedPanels, hasNested := panelMap[\"panels\"].([]interface{})\n\t\tif !hasNested {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, nestedPanel := range nestedPanels {\n\t\t\tnestedPanelMap, ok := nestedPanel.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tupgradeValueMappingsForPanel(nestedPanelMap)\n\t\t\tmigrateTooltipOptions(nestedPanelMap)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// upgradeValueMappingsForPanel migrates value mappings from old format to new format\nfunc upgradeValueMappingsForPanel(panel map[string]interface{}) {\n\tfieldConfig, ok := panel[\"fieldConfig\"].(map[string]interface{})\n\tif !ok {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\t// Upgrade defaults mappings\n\tif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\tif mappings, ok := defaults[\"mappings\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tvar thresholds map[string]interface{}\n\t\t\tif t, ok := defaults[\"thresholds\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\t\tthresholds = t\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\tdefaults[\"mappings\"] = upgradeValueMappings(mappings, thresholds)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Upgrade overrides mappings\n\toverrides, hasOverrides := fieldConfig[\"overrides\"].([]interface{})\n\tif !hasOverrides {\n\t\treturn\n\t}\n\n\tfor _, override := range overrides {\n\t\toverrideMap, ok := override.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tproperties, hasProperties := overrideMap[\"properties\"].([]interface{})\n\t\tif !hasProperties {\n\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t}\n\n\t\tfor _, property := range properties {\n\t\t\tpropertyMap, ok := property.(map[string]interface{})\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tif propertyMap[\"id\"] != \"mappings\" {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tmappings, ok := propertyMap[\"value\"].([]interface{})\n\t\t\tif !ok {\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t}\n\n\t\t\tpropertyMap[\"value\"] = upgradeValueMappings(mappings, nil)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n}\n\n// upgradeValueMappings converts legacy value mappings to new format\nfunc upgradeValueMappings(oldMappings []interface{}, thresholds map[string]interface{}) []interface{} {\n\tif len(oldMappings) == 0 {\n\t\treturn oldMappings\n\t}\n\n\t// Check if all mappings are already in the new format\n\tif areAllMappingsNewFormat(oldMappings) {\n\t\treturn oldMappings\n\t}\n\n\tvalueMaps := createValueMaps()\n\tvar newMappings []interface{}\n\thasValueMappings := false\n\n\tfor _, mapping := range oldMappings {\n\t\tif mappingMap, ok := mapping.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tif processLegacyMapping(mappingMap, thresholds, valueMaps, &newMappings, hasValueMappings)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\t// Add consolidated value mappings at the beginning if any exist\n\tif hasValueMappings {\n\t\tnewMappings = append([]interface{}{valueMaps}, newMappings...)\n\t}\n\n\treturn newMappings\n}\n\n// areAllMappingsNewFormat checks if all mappings are already in the new format\nfunc areAllMappingsNewFormat(oldMappings []interface{}) bool {\n\tfor _, mapping := range oldMappings {\n\t\tif mappingMap, ok := mapping.(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n\t\t\tif mappingType, ok := mappingMap[\"type\"].(string); ok && mappingType != \"\" {\n\t\t\t\t// This is already in new format, keep it as-is\n\t\t\t\tcontinue\n\t\t\t} else {\n\t\t\t\t// Found a legacy format mapping, need to process\n\t\t\t\treturn false\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\treturn true\n}\n\n// createValueMaps creates the base value maps structure\nfunc createValueMaps() map[string]interface{} {\n\treturn isNewFormatMapping(mappingMap map[string]interface{}) bool {\n\tif mappingType, ok := mappingMap[\"type\"].(string); ok && mappingType != \"\" {\n\t\treturn true\n\t}\n\treturn false\n}\n\n// processNewFormatMapping handles mappings that are already in the new format\nfunc processNewFormatMapping(mappingMap map[string]interface{}, valueMaps map[string]interface{}, newMappings *[]interface{}, hasValueMappings bool) bool {\n\tmappingType := mappingMap[\"type\"].(string)\n\tif mappingType == \"value\" {\n\t\t// Consolidate existing value mappings\n\t\tif options, ok := v\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t\thasValueMappings = true\n\t\t}\n\t} else {\n\t\t*newMappings = append(*newMappings, mappingMap)\n\t}\n\treturn hasValueMappings\n}\n\n// processLegacyMapping handles legacy format mappings\nfunc processLegacyMapping(mappingMap map[string]interface{}, thresholds map[string]interface{}, valueMaps map[string]interface{}, newMappings *[]interface{}, hasValueMappings bool) bool {\n\tcolor := getColorFromThresholds(mappingMap, thresholds)\n\n\t// Convert legacy type numbers to new format\n\tif mappingType := GetIntValue(mappingMap, \"type\", -1); mappingType != -1 {\n\t\tswitch mappingType {\n\t\tcase 1: // ValueToText\n\t\t\thasValueMappings = processValueToTextMapping(mappingMap, color, thresholds, valueMaps, newMappings, hasValueMappings)\n\t\tcase 2: // RangeToText\n\t\t\tprocessRangeToTextMapping(mappingMap, color, newMappings)\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn hasValueMappings\n}\n\n// getColorFromThresholds extracts color from thresholds based on mapping text (matches frontend behavior)\nfunc getColorFromThresholds(mappingMap map[string]interface{}, thresholds map[string]interface{}) interface{} {\n\tif thresholds == nil {\n\t\treturn nil\n\t}\n\n\t// Try to get color from threshold based on the mapping text (matches frontend behavior)\n\tif text, ok := mappingMap[\"text\"]; ok {\n\t\tif textStr, ok := text.(string); ok {\n\t\t\tif numeric, err := strconv.ParseFloat(textStr, 64); err == nil {\n\t\t\t\treturn getActiveThresholdColor(numeric, thresholds)\n\t\t\t}\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\n\treturn nil\n}\n\n// processValueToTextMapping handles ValueToText color\n\t}\n\tvalueMapsOptions[stringifyValue(value)] = result\n}\n\n// processRangeToTextMapping handles RangeToText legacy mappings\nfunc processRangeToTextMapping(mappingMap map[string]interface{},   "content": "# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression\n\n## Summary\nThe v38 dashboard schema migration fails to process table panels when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not explicitly defined in the dashboard JSON. This causes field override configuration to be silently skipped during both backend and frontend migration, resulting in loss of column formatting (cell display modes, widths, alignment).\n\n## Root Cause\n\n### Primary Issue: Broken Conditional Logic in V38 Migration\n\n**Backend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`, lines 115-137):\n\n```go\ndefaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue\n}\n\ncustom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\nif !ok {\n    continue  // <-- CRITICAL: Entire panel migration skipped if custom doesn't exist\n}\n\n// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions\nif displayMode, exists := custom[\"displayMode\"]; exists {\n    if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {\n        custom[\"cellOptions\"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)\n    }\n    delete(custom, \"displayMode\")\n}\n\n// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\nmigrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // <-- Never reached if custom doesn't exist\n```\n\nThe type assertion on line 120 (`custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})`) assumes `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` already exists. When it doesn't:\n- The assertion fails (ok == false)\n- The migration skips to the next panel via `continue` (line 122)\n- **Field overrides are never migrated** because `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` (line 135) is never called\n\n**Frontend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`, lines 644-674):\n\n```typescript\nif (oldVersion < 38 && finalTargetVersion >= 38) {\n  panelUpgrades.push((panel: PanelModel) => {\n    if (panel.type === 'table' && panel.fieldConfig !== undefined) {\n      const displayMode = panel.fieldConfig.defaults?.custom?.displayMode;  // <-- Optional chaining\n\n      // Update field configuration\n      if (displayMode !== undefined) {  // <-- Skips if custom doesn't exist\n        panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.cellOptions = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayMode);\n        delete panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom.displayMode;\n      }\n\n      // Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode\n      if (panel.fieldConfig?.overrides) {\n        for (const override of panel.fieldConfig.overrides) {\n          for (let j = 0; j < (override.properties?.length || 0); j++) {\n            if (override.properties[j].id === 'custom.displayMode') {\n              // Override migration happens regardless of defaults.custom\n              override.properties[j].id = 'custom.cellOptions';\n              override.properties[j].value = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(overrideDisplayMode);\n            }\n          }\n        }\n      }\n    }\n    return panel;\n  });\n}\n```\n\nThe optional chaining `?.` on line 647 causes the entire defaults migration to be skipped if `custom` doesn't exist. While overrides migration (lines 659-668) runs independently, it creates an inconsistency: overrides reference `custom.cellOptions` but the defaults object may not have `custom` properly initialized.\n\n### Secondary Issue: Inconsistent Default Structure\n\n**PanelModel Default Definition** (`/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/PanelModel.ts`, lines 130-133):\n\n```typescript\nconst defaults: any = {\n  ...\n  fieldConfig: {\n    defaults: {},      // <-- No 'custom' object initialized\n    overrides: [],\n  },\n  ...\n};\n```\n\nThe default `fieldConfig` structure only initializes `defaults: {}` and `overrides: []`. There is **no `custom` object**. This means:\n\n1. Dashboards created before explicit `custom` properties were added won't have `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n2. Dashboards imported from external sources or created with minimal configuration structures won't have it\n3. The v38 migration assumes this structure will always exist, creating a silent failure\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Test Coverage Gap\n**File**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38_test.go`\n\nAll test cases (lines 9-445) have explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` defined. **Missing test case**: Dashboard with `fieldConfig` but without `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`.\n\nAll test inputs follow this pattern (lines 22-28):\n```go\n\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n    \"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n        \"custom\": map[string]interface{}{  // <-- Always present\n            \"displayMode\": \"basic\",\n        },\n    },\n    \"overrides\": []interface{}{},\n},\n```\n\n**No test covers**:\n```go\n\"fieldConfig\": map[string]interface{}{\n    \"defaults\": map[string]interface{}{\n        // No 'custom' property\n    },\n    \"overrides\": []interface{}{\n        map[string]interface{}{\n            \"properties\": []interface{}{\n                map[string]interface{}{\n                    \"id\":    \"custom.displayMode\",\n                    \"value\": \"gradient-gauge\",\n                },\n            },\n        },\n    },\n},\n```\n\n### Version Progression\n**File**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v30.go` (lines 130-145)\n\nEarlier migrations (v30) handle missing `custom` by checking existence before access:\n\n```go\nif defaults, ok := fieldConfig[\"defaults\"].(map[string]interface{}); ok {\n    if mappings, ok := defaults[\"mappings\"].([]interface{}); ok {\n        // Process mappings\n    }\n}\n```\n\nV30 doesn't assume `custom` exists and processes only fields that are present. **V38 breaks this pattern** by requiring `custom` to exist.\n\n## Affected Components\n\n### Backend Migration Pipeline\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go` (processPanelsV38, migrateOverrides, migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions)\n- **Impact**: Dashboard imports/saves via backend API, schema version advancement\n- **Scope**: All table panels in dashboards where `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not pre-initialized\n\n### Frontend Migration Pipeline\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts` (v38 conditional block, lines 644-674)\n- **Impact**: Dashboard viewing, panel rendering\n- **Scope**: Same as backend, compounded by inconsistency\n\n### Field Configuration Structure\n- **Primary**: `/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/PanelModel.ts` (default fieldConfig definition)\n- **Related**: `/workspace/public/app/plugins/panel/table/migrations.ts` (table panel migrations)\n- **Impact**: How field overrides are stored and serialized\n\n## Affected Schema Version\n- **Version**: 38 (Table cell display configuration migration: displayMode \u2192 cellOptions)\n- **Dashboard Versions**: Affects dashboards at schema version 37 (or earlier) that lack explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n- **Introduced**: Schema migration from v10.3 to v10.4\n- **Regression Type**: Silent data loss (field overrides not migrated)\n\n## Conditional Logic Failure\n\n### Failure Condition\nA dashboard triggers the regression when:\n\n1. **Panel type is 'table'** - Only table panels are processed by v38\n2. **Has fieldConfig** - Panel has field configuration structure\n3. **Has fieldConfig.defaults** - Defaults object exists\n4. **Missing fieldConfig.defaults.custom** - No explicit custom object (common in older/minimal dashboards)\n5. **Has fieldConfig.overrides with custom.displayMode** - Field-specific displayMode overrides exist\n\n### Why Dashboards With Explicit custom Are Unaffected\n\nWhen `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` IS explicitly defined:\n- Type assertion succeeds: `custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})` returns ok=true\n- Migration enters the processing block\n- Both defaults and overrides are correctly migrated\n- displayMode is converted to cellOptions and removed\n\n## Migration Chain\n\n```\nDashboard Schema v37 \u2192 V38 Migration \u2192 Schema v38\n    \u2193                      \u2193\nBackend Processes    Type assertion fails\n(if custom missing)   custom doesn't exist\n    \u2193                  continue to next panel\nDatabase saved    Overrides not migrated\n    \u2193\nFrontend loads       Optional chaining skips\nfrom database        defaults processing\n    \u2193\nRenders with    Overrides may reference\nmissing formatting  non-existent custom.cellOptions\n```\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\nThe v38 migration must initialize `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` if it doesn't exist before processing:\n\n1. **Backend (v38.go)**: Initialize empty custom object if missing\n   ```go\n   custom, ok := defaults[\"custom\"].(map[string]interface{})\n   if !ok {\n       custom = make(map[string]interface{})\n       defaults[\"custom\"] = custom\n   }\n   // Now proceed with migration\n   ```\n\n2. **Frontend (DashboardMigrator.ts)**: Ensure custom object exists before assignment\n   ```typescript\n   if (!panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom) {\n       panel.fieldConfig.defaults.custom = {};\n   }\n   // Now safe to migrate\n   ```\n\n3. **Test Coverage**: Add test case for dashboards without explicit `fieldConfig.defaults.custom`\n\n4. **Consistency**: Review other migrations (v30, v35, v42) to ensure they follow the same pattern of initializing missing structures rather than skipping them\n\n### Prevention\n- All future schema migrations should validate/initialize required object structures before processing\n- Test coverage should include both \"structure exists\" and \"structure missing\" scenarios\n- Consider adding schema validation in the migration framework to catch these patterns early\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report: Dashboard Migration v38 Table Panel Regression

## Summary
The v38 dashboard schema migration fails to process table panels when `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` is not explicitly defined in the dashboard JSON. This causes field override configuration to be silently skipped during both backend and frontend migration, resulting in loss of column formatting (cell display modes, widths, alignment).

## Root Cause

### Primary Issue: Broken Conditional Logic in V38 Migration

**Backend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/apps/dashboard/pkg/migration/schemaversion/v38.go`, lines 115-137):

```go
defaults, ok := fieldConfig["defaults"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue
}

custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})
if !ok {
    continue  // <-- CRITICAL: Entire panel migration skipped if custom doesn't exist
}

// Migrate displayMode to cellOptions
if displayMode, exists := custom["displayMode"]; exists {
    if displayModeStr, ok := displayMode.(string); ok {
        custom["cellOptions"] = migrateTableDisplayModeToCellOptions(displayModeStr)
    }
    delete(custom, "displayMode")
}

// Update any overrides referencing the cell display mode
migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)  // <-- Never reached if custom doesn't exist
```

The type assertion on line 120 (`custom, ok := defaults["custom"].(map[string]interface{})`) assumes `fieldConfig.defaults.custom` already exists. When it doesn't:
- The assertion fails (ok == false)
- The migration skips to the next panel via `continue` (line 122)
- **Field overrides are never migrated** because `migrateOverrides(fieldConfig)` (line 135) is never called

**Frontend v38 Migration** (`/workspace/public/app/features/dashboard/state/DashboardMigrator.ts`, lines 644-674):

```typescript
if (oldVersion < 3
... (truncated)
